<li>
<h3>A Layer 2 switch is used to switch incoming frames from a 1000BASE-T port to a port connected to a 100Base-T network. Which method of memory buffering would work best for this task?</h3>
<ul>
<li>port-based buffering</li>
<li>level 1 cache buffering</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">shared memory buffering</span></li>
<li>fixed configuration buffering<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>With shared memory buffering, the number of frames stored in the buffer is restricted only by the of the entire memory buffer and not limited to a single port buffer. This permits larger frames to be transmitted with fewer dropped frames. This is important to asymmetric switching, which applies to this scenario, where frames are being exchanged between ports of different rates. With port-based memory buffering, frames are stored in queues that are linked to specific incoming and outgoing ports making it possible for a single frame to delay the transmission of all the frames in memory because of a busy destination port. Level 1 cache is memory used in a CPU. Fixed configuration refers to the port arrangement in switch hardware.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What are two examples of the cut-through switching method? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li>store-and-forward switching</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">fast-forward switching</span></li>
<li>CRC switching</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">fragment-free switching</span></li>
<li>QOS switching<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Store-and forward switching accepts the entire frame and performs error checking using CRC before forwarding the frame. Store-and-forward is often required for QOS analysis. Fast-forward and fragment-free are both variations of the cut-through switching method where only part of the frame is received before the switch begins to forward it.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which frame forwarding method receives the entire frame and performs a CRC check to detect errors before forwarding the frame?</h3>
<ul>
<li>cut-through switching</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">store-and-forward switching</span></li>
<li>fragment-free switching</li>
<li>fast-forward switching<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Fast-forward and fragment-free switching are variations of cut-through switching, which begins to forward the frame before the entire frame is received.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What is the purpose of the FCS field in a frame?</h3>
<ul>
<li>to obtain the MAC address of the sending node</li>
<li>to verify the logical address of the sending node</li>
<li>to compute the CRC header for the data field</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">to determine if errors occurred in the transmission and reception</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The FCS field in a frame is used to detect any errors in the transmission and receipt of a frame. This is done by comparing the CRC value within the frame against a computed CRC value of the frame. If the two values do not match, then the frame is discarded.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which switching method has the lowest level of latency?</h3>
<ul>
<li>cut-through</li>
<li>store-and-forward</li>
<li>fragment-free</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">fast-forward</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Fast-forward switching begins to forward a frame after reading the destination MAC address, resulting in the lowest latency. Fragment-free reads the first 64 bytes before forwarding. Store-and-forward has the highest latency because it reads the entire frame before beginning to forward it. Both fragment-free and fast-forward are types of cut-through switching.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>A network administrator is connecting two modern switches using a straight-through cable. The switches are new and have never been configured. Which three statements are correct about the final result of the connection? (Choose three.)</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The link between the switches will work at the fastest speed that is supported by both switches.</span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The link between switches will work as full-duplex.</span></li>
<li>If both switches support different speeds, they will each work at their own fastest speed.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The auto-MDIX feature will configure the interfaces eliminating the need for a crossover cable.</span></li>
<li>The connection will not be possible unless the administrator changes the cable to a crossover cable.</li>
<li>The duplex capability has to be manually configured because it cannot be negotiated.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Modern switches can negotiate to work in full-duplex mode if both switches are capable. They will negotiate to work using the fastest possible speed and the auto-MDIX feature is enabled by default, so a cable change is not needed.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which advantage does the store-and-forward switching method have compared with the cut-through switching method?</h3>
<ul>
<li>collision detecting</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">frame error checking</span></li>
<li>faster frame forwarding</li>
<li>frame forwarding using IPv4 Layer 3 and 4 information<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>A switch using the store-and-forward switching method performs an error check on an incoming frame by comparing the FCS value against its own FCS calculations after the entire frame is received. In comparison, a switch using the cut-through switching method makes quick forwarding decisions and starts the forwarding process without waiting for the entire frame to be received. Thus a switch using cut-through switching may send invalid frames to the network. The performance of store-and-forward switching is slower compared to cut-through switching performance. Collision detection is monitored by the sending device. Store-and-forward switching does not use IPv4 Layer 3 and 4 information for its forwarding decisions.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>When the store-and-forward method of switching is in use, what part of the Ethernet frame is used to perform an error check?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">CRC in the trailer</span></li>
<li>source MAC address in the header</li>
<li>destination MAC address in the header</li>
<li>protocol type in the header<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The cyclic redundancy check (CRC) part of the trailer is used to determine if the frame has been modified during transit.​ If the integrity of the frame is verified, the frame is forwarded. If the integrity of the frame cannot be verified, then the frame is dropped.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which switching method uses the CRC value in a frame?</h3>
<ul>
<li>cut-through</li>
<li>fast-forward</li>
<li>fragment-free</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">store-and-forward</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>When the store-and-forward switching method is used, the switch receives the complete frame before forwarding it on to the destination. The cyclic redundancy check (CRC) part of the trailer is used to determine if the frame has been modified during transit.​​ In contrast, a cut-through switch forwards the frame once the destination Layer 2 address is read. Two types of cut-through switching methods are fast-forward and fragment-free.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What are two actions performed by a Cisco switch? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li>building a routing table that is based on the first IP address in the frame header</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">using the source MAC addresses of frames to build and maintain a MAC address table</span></li>
<li>forwarding frames with unknown destination IP addresses to the default gateway</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">utilizing the MAC address table to forward frames via the destination MAC address</span></li>
<li>examining the destination MAC address to add new entries to the MAC address table<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Important actions that a switch performs are as follows:When a frame comes in, the switch examines the Layer 2 source address to build and maintain the Layer 2 MAC address table.<br />
It examines the Layer 2 destination address to determine how to forward the frame. When the destination address is in the MAC address table, then the frame is sent out a particular port. When the address is unknown, the frame is sent to all ports that have devices connected to that network.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which two statements describe features or functions of the logical link control sublayer in Ethernet standards? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Logical link control is implemented in software.</span></li>
<li>Logical link control is specified in the IEEE 802.3 standard.</li>
<li>The LLC sublayer adds a header and a trailer to the data.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The data link layer uses LLC to communicate with the upper layers of the protocol suite.</span></li>
<li>The LLC sublayer is responsible for the placement and retrieval of frames on and off the media.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Logical link control is implemented in software and enables the data link layer to communicate with the upper layers of the protocol suite. Logical link control is specified in the IEEE 802.2 standard. IEEE 802.3 is a suite of standards that define the different Ethernet types. The MAC (Media Access Control) sublayer is responsible for the placement and retrieval of frames on and off the media. The MAC sublayer is also responsible for adding a header and a trailer to the network layer protocol data unit (PDU).</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What is the auto-MDIX feature?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">It enables a device to automatically configure an interface to use a straight-through or a crossover cable.</span></li>
<li>It enables a device to automatically configure the duplex settings of a segment.</li>
<li>It enables a device to automatically configure the speed of its interface.</li>
<li>It enables a switch to dynamically select the forwarding method.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The auto-MDIX feature allows the device to configure its network port according to the cable type that is used (straight-through or crossover) and the type of device that is connected to that port. When a port of a switch is configured with auto-MDIX, this switch can be connected to another switch by the use of either a straight-through cable or a crossover cable.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What is one advantage of using the cut-through switching method instead of the store-and-forward switching method?</h3>
<ul>
<li>has a positive impact on bandwidth by dropping most of the invalid frames</li>
<li>makes a fast forwarding decision based on the source MAC address of the frame</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">has a lower latency appropriate for high-performance computing applications​</span></li>
<li>provides the flexibility to support any mix of Ethernet speeds<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Cut-through switching provides lower latency switching for high-performance computing (HPC) applications. Cut-through switching allows more invalid frames to cross the network than store-and-forward switching. The cut-through switching method can make a forwarding decision as soon as it looks up the destination MAC address of the frame.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which is a multicast MAC address?</h3>
<ul>
<li>FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF</li>
<li>5C-26-0A-4B-19-3E</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">01-00-5E-00-00-03</span></li>
<li>00-26-0F-4B-00-3E<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Multicast MAC addresses begin with the special value of 01-00-5E.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>

<h3>Refer to the exhibit. What is wrong with the displayed termination?</h3>

<ul>
<li>The woven copper braid should not have been removed.</li>
<li>The wrong type of connector is being used.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The untwisted length of each wire is too long. </span></li>
<li>The wires are too thick for the connector that is used.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>When a cable to an RJ-45 connector is terminated, it is important to ensure that the untwisted wires are not too long and that the flexible plastic sheath surrounding the wires is crimped down and not the bare wires. None of the colored wires should be visible from the bottom of the jack.</p>
</td>
</tr>

<li>
<h3>Refer to the exhibit. The PC is connected to the console port of the switch. All the other connections are made through FastEthernet links. Which types of UTP cables can be used to connect the devices?​</h3>
<figure id="attachment_213" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-213" style="width: 637px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-213" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20637%20134'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="CCNA1 v7 – ITNv7 – Modules 4 – 7 Ethernet Concepts Exam Answers 05" width="637" height="134" data-lazy-srcset="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-–-ITNv7-–-Modules-4-–-7-Ethernet-Concepts-Exam-Answers-05-1.jpg 637w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-–-ITNv7-–-Modules-4-–-7-Ethernet-Concepts-Exam-Answers-05-1-300x63.jpg 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 637px) 100vw, 637px" data-lazy-src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-–-ITNv7-–-Modules-4-–-7-Ethernet-Concepts-Exam-Answers-05-1.jpg" /><noscript><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-213" src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-–-ITNv7-–-Modules-4-–-7-Ethernet-Concepts-Exam-Answers-05-1.jpg" alt="CCNA1 v7 – ITNv7 – Modules 4 – 7 Ethernet Concepts Exam Answers 05" width="637" height="134" srcset="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-–-ITNv7-–-Modules-4-–-7-Ethernet-Concepts-Exam-Answers-05-1.jpg 637w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-–-ITNv7-–-Modules-4-–-7-Ethernet-Concepts-Exam-Answers-05-1-300x63.jpg 300w" sizes="(max-width: 637px) 100vw, 637px" /></noscript><figcaption id="caption-attachment-213" class="wp-caption-text">CCNA1 v7 – ITNv7 – Modules 4 – 7 Ethernet Concepts Exam Answers 05</figcaption></figure>
<ul>
<li>1 &#8211; rollover, 2 &#8211; crossover, 3 &#8211; straight-through</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">1 &#8211; rollover, 2 &#8211; straight-through, 3 &#8211; crossover</span></li>
<li>1 &#8211; crossover, 2 &#8211; straight-through, 3 &#8211; rollover</li>
<li>1 &#8211; crossover, 2 &#8211; rollover, 3 &#8211; straight-through<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>A straight-through cable is commonly used to interconnect a host to a switch and a switch to a router. A crossover cable is used to interconnect similar devices together like switch to a switch, a host to a host, or a router to a router. If a switch has the MDIX capability, a crossover could be used to connect the switch to the router; however, that option is not available. A rollover cable is used to connect to a router or switch console port.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>

<h3>Which port does Switch0 use to send frames to the host with the IPv4 address 10.1.1.5?</h3>
<ul>
<li>Fa0/1</li>
<li>Fa0/5</li>
<li>Fa0/9</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Fa0/11</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Issuing the command i pconfig /all from the PC0 command prompt displays the IPv4 address and MAC address. When the IPv4 address 10.1.1.5 is pinged from PC0, the switch stores the source MAC address (from PC0) along with the port to which PC0 is connected. When the destination reply is received, the switch takes the destination MAC address and compares to MAC addresses stored in the MAC address table. Issuing the show mac-address-table on the PC0 Terminal application displays two dynamic MAC address entries. The MAC address and port entry that does not belong to PC0 must be the MAC address and port of the destination with the IPv4 address 10.1.1.5.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What does the term &#8220;attenuation&#8221; mean in data communication?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">loss of signal strength as distance increases</span></li>
<li>time for a signal to reach its destination</li>
<li>leakage of signals from one cable pair to another</li>
<li>strengthening of a signal by a networking device<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Data is transmitted on copper cables as electrical pulses. A detector in the network interface of a destination device must receive a signal that can be successfully decoded to match the signal sent. However, the farther the signal travels, the more it deteriorates. This is referred to as signal attenuation.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What makes fiber preferable to copper cabling for interconnecting buildings? (Choose three.)</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">greater distances per cable run</span></li>
<li>lower installation cost</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">limited susceptibility to EMI/RFI</span></li>
<li>durable connections</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">greater bandwidth potential</span></li>
<li>easily terminated<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Optical fiber cable transmits data over longer distances and at higher bandwidths than any other networking media. Unlike copper wires, fiber-optic cable can transmit signals with less attenuation and is completely immune to EMI and RFI.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Implements a trailer to detect transmission errors. </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Controls the NIC responsible for sending and receiving data on the physical medium.</span></li>
<li>Places information in the frame that identifies which network layer protocol is being used for the frame.</li>
<li>Adds Layer 2 control information to network protocol data.</li>
<li>Enables IPv4 and IPv6 to utilize the same network interface and media.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Places information in the frame that identifies which network layer protocol is being used for the frame.</span></li>
<li>Integrates various physical technologies.</li>
<li>Implements a process to delimit fields within a Layer 2 frame.</li>
<li>Controls the NIC responsible for sending and receiving data on the physical medium.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Controls the NIC responsible for sending and receiving data on the physical medium.</span></li>
<li>Places information in the frame that identifies which network layer protocol is being used for the frame.</li>
<li>Adds Layer 2 control information to network protocol data.</li>
<li>Communicates between the networking software at the upper layers and the device hardware at the lower layers.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Adds Layer 2 control information to network protocol data. </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Enables IPv4 and IPv6 to utilize the same network interface and media.</span></li>

<li>Implements a trailer to detect transmission errors.</li>
<li>Provides synchronization between source and target nodes.</li>

<li>
<h3>Which two functions are performed at the MAC sublayer of the OSI data link layer? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Implements a trailer to detect transmission errors. </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Provides synchronization between source and target nodes.</span></li>
<li>Places information in the frame that identifies which network layer protocol is being used for the frame.</li>
<li>Enables IPv4 and IPv6 to utilize the same network interface and media.</li>
<li>Adds Layer 2 control information to network protocol data.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which two functions are performed at the LLC sublayer of the OSI data link layer? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Enables IPv4 and IPv6 to utilize the same network interface and media. </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Adds Layer 2 control information to network protocol data.</span></li>
<li>Integrates various physical technologies.</li>
<li>Implements a trailer to detect transmission errors.</li>
<li>Provides synchronization between source and target nodes.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which two functions are performed at the MAC sublayer of the OSI data link layer? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Provides a mechanism to allow multiple devices to communicate over a shared medium. </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Controls the NIC responsible for sending and receiving data on the physical medium.</span></li>
<li>Places information in the frame that identifies which network layer protocol is being used for the frame.</li>
<li>Adds Layer 2 control information to network protocol data.</li>
<li>Enables IPv4 and IPv6 to utilize the same network interface and media.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a switch receives a frame and does have the source MAC address in the MAC table?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The switch refreshes the timer on that entry.</span></li>
<li>The switch shares the MAC address table entry with any connected switches.</li>
<li>The switch does not forward the frame.</li>
<li>The switch sends the frame to a connected router because the destination MAC address is not local.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a switch receives a frame with the destination MAC address FF:FF:FF:FF:FF:FF?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The switch forwards it out all ports except the ingress port.</span></li>
<li>The switch shares the MAC address table entry with any connected switches.</li>
<li>The switch does not forward the frame.</li>
<li>The switch sends the frame to a connected router because the destination MAC address is not local.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a host receives a frame with a destination MAC address it does not recognize?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The host will discard the frame.</span></li>
<li>The host sends the frame to the switch to update the MAC address table.</li>
<li>The host forwards the frame to the router.</li>
<li>The host forwards the frame to all other hosts.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a switch receives a frame with the destination MAC address 01:00:5E:00:00:D9?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The switch forwards it out all ports except the ingress port.</span></li>
<li>The switch does not forward the frame.</li>
<li>The switch sends the frame to a connected router because the destination MAC address is not local.</li>
<li>The switch shares the MAC address table entry with any connected switches.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a host receives a frame with a destination MAC address of FF:FF:FF:FF:FF:FF?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The host will process the frame.</span></li>
<li>The host forwards the frame to the router.</li>
<li>The host sends the frame to the switch to update the MAC address table.</li>
<li>The host forwards the frame to all other hosts.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a switch receives a frame and does have the source MAC address in the MAC table?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The switch refreshes the timer on that entry.</span></li>
<li>The switch adds it to its MAC address table associated with the port number.</li>
<li>The switch forwards the frame to the associated port.</li>
<li>The switch sends the frame to a connected router because the destination MAC address is not local.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a host receives a frame with a destination MAC address of FF:FF:FF:FF:FF:FF?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The host will process the frame.</span></li>
<li>The host returns the frame to the switch.</li>
<li>The host replies to the switch with its own IP address.</li>
<li>The host forwards the frame to all other hosts.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a switch receives a frame and does have the source MAC address in the MAC table?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The switch refreshes the timer on that entry.</span></li>
<li>The switch shares the MAC address table entry with any connected switches.</li>
<li>The switch does not forward the frame.</li>
<li>The switch adds it to its MAC address table associated with the port number.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a host receives a frame with a destination MAC address it does not recognize?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The host will discard the frame.</span></li>
<li>The host replies to the switch with its own IP address.</li>
<li>The host forwards the frame to all other hosts.</li>
<li>The host returns the frame to the switch.</li>
</ul>

<li>
<h3>What action will occur if a switch receives a frame with the destination MAC address FF:FF:FF:FF:FF:FF?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The switch forwards it out all ports except the ingress port.</span></li>
<li>The switch refreshes the timer on that entry.</li>
<li>The switch does not forward the frame.</li>
<li>The switch sends the frame to a connected router because the destination MAC address is not local.</li>

<li>
<h3>A computer can access devices on the same network but cannot access devices on other networks. What is the probable cause of this problem?</h3>
<ul>
<li>The cable is not connected properly to the NIC.</li>
<li>The computer has an invalid IP address.</li>
<li>The computer has an incorrect subnet mask.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><span style="color: #ff0000;">The computer has an invalid default gateway address.</span></span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The default gateway is the address of the device a host uses to access the Internet or another network. If the default gateway is missing or incorrect, that host will not be able to communicate outside the local network. Because the host can access other hosts on the local network, the network cable and the other parts of the IP configuration are working.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which statement describes a feature of the IP protocol?</h3>
<ul>
<li>IP encapsulation is modified based on network media.</li>
<li>IP relies on Layer 2 protocols for transmission error control.</li>
<li>MAC addresses are used during the IP packet encapsulation.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">IP relies on upper layer services to handle situations of missing or out-of-order packets.</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>IP protocol is a connection-less protocol, considered unreliable in terms of end-to-end delivery. It does not provide error control in the cases where receiving packets are out-of-order or in cases of missing packets. It relies on upper layer services, such as TCP, to resolve these issues.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Why is NAT not needed in IPv6?​</h3>
<ul>
<li>Because IPv6 has integrated security, there is no need to hide the IPv6 addresses of internal networks.​</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Any host or user can get a public IPv6 network address because the number of available IPv6 addresses is extremely large.​</span></li>
<li>The problems that are induced by NAT applications are solved because the IPv6 header improves packet handling by intermediate routers.​</li>
<li>The end-to-end connectivity problems that are caused by NAT are solved because the number of routes increases with the number of nodes that are connected to the Internet.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The large number of public IPv6 addresses eliminates the need for NAT. Sites from the largest enterprises to single households can get public IPv6 network addresses. This avoids some of the NAT-induced application problems that are experienced by applications that require end-to-end connectivity.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which parameter does the router use to choose the path to the destination when there are multiple routes available?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">the lower metric value that is associated with the destination network</span></li>
<li>the lower gateway IP address to get to the destination network</li>
<li>the higher metric value that is associated with the destination network</li>
<li>the higher gateway IP address to get to the destination network<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>When a packet arrives at the router interface, the router examines its header to determine the destination network. If there is a route for the destination network in the routing table, the router forwards the packet using that information. If there are two or more possible routes to the same destination, the metric is used to decide which route appears on the routing table. The lower the metric, the better the route.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>

<ul>
<li>performing error detection</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">routing packets toward the destination</span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">encapsulating PDUs from the transport layer</span></li>
<li>placement of frames on the media</li>
<li>collision detection<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The OSI network layer provides several services to allow communication between devices:addressing<br />
encapsulation<br />
routing<br />
de-encapsulation<br />
Error detection, placing frames on the media, and collision detection are all functions of the data ink layer.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>

<li>
<h3>Within a production network, what is the purpose of configuring a switch with a default gateway address?</h3>
<ul>
<li>Hosts that are connected to the switch can use the switch default gateway address to forward packets to a remote destination.</li>
<li>A switch must have a default gateway to be accessible by Telnet and SSH.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The default gateway address is used to forward packets originating from the switch to remote networks.</span></li>
<li>It provides a next-hop address for all traffic that flows through the switch.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>A default gateway address allows a switch to forward packets that originate on the switch to remote networks. A default gateway address on a switch does not provide Layer 3 routing for PCs that are connected on that switch. A switch can still be accessible from Telnet as long as the source of the Telnet connection is on the local network.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What is a basic characteristic of the IP protocol?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">connectionless</span></li>
<li>media dependent</li>
<li>user data segmentation</li>
<li>reliable end-to-end delivery<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Internet Protocol (IP) is a network layer protocol that does not require initial exchange of control information to establish an end-to-end connection before packets are forwarded. Thus, IP is connectionless and does not provide reliable end-to-end delivery by itself. IP is media independent. User data segmentation is a service provided at the transport layer.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which field in the IPv4 header is used to prevent a packet from traversing a network endlessly?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Time-to-Live</span></li>
<li>Sequence Number</li>
<li>Acknowledgment Number</li>
<li>Differentiated Services<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The value of the Time-to-Live (TTL) field in the IPv4 header is used to limit the lifetime of a packet. The sending host sets the initial TTL value; which is decreased by one each time the packet is processed by a router. If the TTL field decrements to zero, the router discards the packet and sends an Internet Control Message Protocol (ICMP) Time Exceeded message to the source IP address. The Differentiated Services (DS) field is used to determine the priority of each packet. Sequence Number and Acknowledgment Number are two fields in the TCP header.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What is one advantage that the IPv6 simplified header offers over IPv4?</h3>
<ul>
<li>smaller-sized header</li>
<li>little requirement for processing checksums</li>
<li>smaller-sized source and destination IP addresses</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">efficient packet handling</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The IPv6 simplified header offers several advantages over IPv4:<br />
· Better routing efficiency and efficient packet handling for performance and forwarding-rate scalability<br />
· No requirement for processing checksums<br />
· Simplified and more efficient extension header mechanisms (as opposed to the IPv4 Options field)<br />
· A Flow Label field for per-flow processing with no need to open the transport inner packet to identify the various traffic flows</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What IPv4 header field identifies the upper layer protocol carried in the packet?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Protocol</span></li>
<li>Identification</li>
<li>Version</li>
<li>Differentiated Services<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>It is the Protocol field in the IP header that identifies the upper-layer protocol the packet is carrying. The Version field identifies the IP version. The Differential Services field is used for setting packet priority. The Identification field is used to reorder fragmented packets.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>

<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Packets with a destination of 172.17.6.15 are forwarded through Fa0/0. Packets with a destination of 172.17.10.5 are forwarded through Fa1/1. Packets with a destination of 172.17.12.10 are forwarded through Fa1/0. Packets with a destination of 172.17.14.8 are forwarded through Fa0/1. Because network 172.17.8.0 has no entry in the routing table, it will take the gateway of last resort, which means that packets with a destination of 172.17.8.20 are forwarded through Serial0/0/0. Because a gateway of last resort exists, no packets will be dropped.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<li>
<h3>What information does the loopback test provide?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The TCP/IP stack on the device is working correctly.</span></li>
<li>The device has end-to-end connectivity.</li>
<li>DHCP is working correctly.</li>
<li>The Ethernet cable is working correctly.</li>
<li>The device has the correct IP address on the network.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Because the loopback test sends packets back to the host device, it does not provide information about network connectivity to other hosts. The loopback test verifies that the host NIC, drivers, and TCP/IP stack are functioning.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What routing table entry has a next hop address associated with a destination network?</h3>
<ul>
<li>directly-connected routes</li>
<li>local routes</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">remote routes</span></li>
<li>C and L source routes<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Routing table entries for remote routes will have a next hop IP address. The next hop IP address is the address of the router interface of the next device to be used to reach the destination network. Directly-connected and local routes have no next hop, because they do not require going through another router to be reached.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>How do hosts ensure that their packets are directed to the correct network destination?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">They have to keep their own local routing table that contains a route to the loopback interface, a local network route, and a remote default route.​</span></li>
<li>They always direct their packets to the default gateway, which will be responsible for the packet delivery.</li>
<li>They search in their own local routing table for a route to the network destination address and pass this information to the default gateway.</li>
<li>They send a query packet to the default gateway asking for the best route.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Hosts must maintain their own local routing table to ensure that network layer packets are directed to the correct destination network. This local table typically contains a route to the loopback interface, a route to the network that the host is connected to, and a local default route, which represents the route that packets must take to reach all remote network addresses.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>When transporting data from real-time applications, such as streaming audio and video, which field in the IPv6 header can be used to inform the routers and switches to maintain the same path for the packets in the same conversation?</h3>
<ul>
<li>Next Header</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Flow Label</span></li>
<li>Traffic Class</li>
<li>Differentiated Services<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The Flow Label in IPv6 header is a 20-bit field that provides a special service for real-time applications. This field can be used to inform routers and switches to maintain the same path for the packet flow so that packets will not be reordered.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What statement describes the function of the Address Resolution Protocol?</h3>
<ul>
<li>ARP is used to discover the IP address of any host on a different network.</li>
<li>ARP is used to discover the IP address of any host on the local network.</li>
<li>ARP is used to discover the MAC address of any host on a different network.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">ARP is used to discover the MAC address of any host on the local network.</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>When a PC wants to send data on the network, it always knows the IP address of the destination. However, it also needs to discover the MAC address of the destination. ARP is the protocol that is used to discover the MAC address of a host that belongs to the same network.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Under which two circumstances will a switch flood a frame out of every port except the port that the frame was received on? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The frame has the broadcast address as the destination address.</span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The destination address is unknown to the switch.</span></li>
<li>The source address in the frame header is the broadcast address.</li>
<li>The source address in the frame is a multicast address.</li>
<li>The destination address in the frame is a known unicast address.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>A switch will flood a frame out of every port, except the one that the frame was received from, under two circumstances. Either the frame has the broadcast address as the destination address, or the destination address is unknown to the switch.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which statement describes the treatment of ARP requests on the local link?</h3>
<ul>
<li>They must be forwarded by all routers on the local network.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">They are received and processed by every device on the local network.</span></li>
<li>They are dropped by all switches on the local network.</li>
<li>They are received and processed only by the target device.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>One of the negative issues with ARP requests is that they are sent as a broadcast. This means all devices on the local link must receive and process the request.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which destination address is used in an ARP request frame?</h3>
<ul>
<li>0.0.0.0</li>
<li>255.255.255.255</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">FFFF.FFFF.FFFF</span></li>
<li>AAAA.AAAA.AAAA</li>
<li>the physical address of the destination host<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The purpose of an ARP request is to find the MAC address of the destination host on an Ethernet LAN. The ARP process sends a Layer 2 broadcast to all devices on the Ethernet LAN. The frame contains the IP address of the destination and the broadcast MAC address, FFFF.FFFF.FFFF. The host with the IP address that matches the IP address in the ARP request will reply with a unicast frame that includes the MAC address of the host. Thus the original sending host will obtain the destination IP and MAC address pair to continue the encapsulation process for data transmission.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>A network technician issues the arp -d * command on a PC after the router that is connected to the LAN is reconfigured. What is the result after this command is issued?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The ARP cache is cleared.</span></li>
<li>The current content of the ARP cache is displayed.</li>
<li>The detailed information of the ARP cache is displayed.</li>
<li>The ARP cache is synchronized with the router interface.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Issuing the arp –d * command on a PC will clear the ARP cache content. This is helpful when a network technician wants to ensure the cache is populated with updated information.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Refer to the exhibit. The exhibit shows a small switched network and the contents of the MAC address table of the switch. PC1 has sent a frame addressed to PC3. What will the switch do with the frame?</h3>
<figure id="attachment_229" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-229" style="width: 583px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-229" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20583%20357'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="CCNA1 v7 - ITNv7 - Modules 8 - 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 04" width="583" height="357" data-lazy-srcset="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-04.png 583w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-04-300x184.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 583px) 100vw, 583px" data-lazy-src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-04.png" /><noscript><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-229" src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-04.png" alt="CCNA1 v7 - ITNv7 - Modules 8 - 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 04" width="583" height="357" srcset="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-04.png 583w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-04-300x184.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 583px) 100vw, 583px" /></noscript><figcaption id="caption-attachment-229" class="wp-caption-text">CCNA1 v7 &#8211; ITNv7 &#8211; Modules 8 &#8211; 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 04</figcaption></figure>
<ul>
<li>The switch will discard the frame.</li>
<li>The switch will forward the frame only to port 2.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The switch will forward the frame to all ports except port 4.</span></li>
<li>The switch will forward the frame to all ports.</li>
<li>The switch will forward the frame only to ports 1 and 3.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The MAC address of PC3 is not present in the MAC table of the switch. Because the switch does not know where to send the frame that is addressed to PC3, it will forward the frame to all the switch ports, except for port 4, which is the incoming port.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Which two types of IPv6 messages are used in place of ARP for address resolution?</h3>
<ul>
<li>anycast</li>
<li>broadcast</li>
<li>echo reply</li>
<li>echo request</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">neighbor solicitation </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">neighbor advertisement</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>IPv6 does not use ARP. Instead, ICMPv6 neighbor discovery is used by sending neighbor solicitation and neighbor advertisement messages.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What is the aim of an ARP spoofing attack?</h3>
<ul>
<li>to flood the network with ARP reply broadcasts</li>
<li>to fill switch MAC address tables with bogus addresses</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">to associate IP addresses to the wrong MAC address</span></li>
<li>to overwhelm network hosts with ARP requests<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>In an ARP spoofing attack, a malicious host intercepts ARP requests and replies to them so that network hosts will map an IP address to the MAC address of the malicious host.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Refer to the exhibit. PC1 attempts to connect to File_server1 and sends an ARP request to obtain a destination MAC address. Which MAC address will PC1 receive in the ARP reply?</h3>
<figure id="attachment_227" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-227" style="width: 365px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-227" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20365%20280'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="CCNA1 v7 - ITNv7 - Modules 8 - 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 03" width="365" height="280" data-lazy-src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-03.gif" /><noscript><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-227" src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-03.gif" alt="CCNA1 v7 - ITNv7 - Modules 8 - 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 03" width="365" height="280" /></noscript><figcaption id="caption-attachment-227" class="wp-caption-text">CCNA1 v7 &#8211; ITNv7 &#8211; Modules 8 &#8211; 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 03</figcaption></figure>
<ul>
<li>the MAC address of S1</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">the MAC address of the G0/0 interface on R1</span></li>
<li>the MAC address of the G0/0 interface on R2</li>
<li>the MAC address of S2</li>
<li>the MAC address of File_server1<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>PC1 must have a MAC address to use as a destination Layer 2 address. PC1 will send an ARP request as a broadcast and R1 will send back an ARP reply with its G0/0 interface MAC address. PC1 can then forward the packet to the MAC address of the default gateway, R1.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Where are IPv4 address to Layer 2 Ethernet address mappings maintained on a host computer?</h3>
<ul>
<li>neighbor table</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">ARP cache</span></li>
<li>routing table</li>
<li>MAC address table<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The ARP cache is used to store IPv4 addresses and the Ethernet physical addresses or MAC addresses to which the IPv4 addresses are mapped. Incorrect mappings of IP addresses to MAC addresses can result in loss of end-to-end connectivity.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What important information is examined in the Ethernet frame header by a Layer 2 device in order to forward the data onward?</h3>
<ul>
<li>source MAC address</li>
<li>source IP address</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">destination MAC address</span></li>
<li>Ethernet type</li>
<li>destination IP address<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The Layer 2 device, such as a switch, uses the destination MAC address to determine which path (interface or port) should be used to send the data onward to the destination device.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>

<h3>Match the commands to the correct actions. (Not all options are used.)</h3>

<li>
<h3>A new network administrator has been asked to enter a banner message on a Cisco device. What is the fastest way a network administrator could test whether the banner is properly configured?</h3>
<ul>
<li>Reboot the device.</li>
<li>Enter CTRL-Z at the privileged mode prompt.</li>
<li>Exit global configuration mode.</li>
<li>Power cycle the device.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Exit privileged EXEC mode and press Enter.</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>While at the privileged mode prompt such as Router#, type exit ,press Enter , and the banner message appears. Power cycling a network device that has had the banner motd command issued will also display the banner message, but this is not a quick way to test the configuration.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>

<li>
<h3>A network administrator requires access to manage routers and switches locally and remotely. Match the description to the access method. (Not all options are used.)</h3>
<figure id="attachment_232" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-232" style="width: 1819px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-232" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201819%201129'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="CCNA1 v7 - ITNv7 - Modules 8 - 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 003" width="1819" height="1129" data-lazy-srcset="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-003-1.jpg 1819w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-003-1-300x186.jpg 300w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-003-1-1024x636.jpg 1024w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-003-1-768x477.jpg 768w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-003-1-1536x953.jpg 1536w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1819px) 100vw, 1819px" data-lazy-src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-003-1.jpg" /><noscript><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-232" src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-003-1.jpg" alt="CCNA1 v7 - <table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Both the console and AUX ports can be used to directly connect to a Cisco network device for management purposes. However, it is more common to use the console port. The AUX port is more often used for remote access via a dial up connection. SSH and Telnet are both remote access methods that depend on an active network connection. SSH uses a stronger password authentication than Telnet uses and also uses encryption on transmitted data.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<li>
<h3>Match the phases to the functions during the boot up process of a Cisco router. (Not all options are used.)</h3>
<figure id="attachment_233" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-233" style="width: 1846px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-233" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201846%20914'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="CCNA1 v7 - ITNv7 - Modules 8 - 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 004" width="1846" height="914" data-lazy-srcset="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-004-1.jpg 1846w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-004-1-300x149.jpg 300w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-004-1-1024x507.jpg 1024w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-004-1-768x380.jpg 768w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-004-1-1536x761.jpg 1536w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1846px) 100vw, 1846px" data-lazy-src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-004-1.jpg" /><noscript><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-233" src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-004-1.jpg" alt="CCNA1 v7 - <table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>There are three major phases to the bootup process of a Cisco router:</p>
<ol>
<li>Perform the POST and load the bootstrap program.</li>
<li>Locate and load the Cisco IOS software.</li>
<li>Locate and load the startup configuration file</li>
</ol>
<p>If a startup configuration file cannot be located, the router will enter setup mode by displaying the setup mode prompt.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
<li>
<h3>Match the command with the device mode at which the command is entered. (Not all options are used.)</h3>

<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>

The <b>ip address 192.168.4.4 255.255.255.0</b> command is entered in R1(config-if)# mode. The <b>service password-encryption</b> command is entered in global configuration mode.</p>

<ul>
<li>The switch will have a management interface with the address 172.16.100.1.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The switch can be remotely managed from a host on another network.</span></li>
<li>The switch can communicate with other hosts on the 172.16.100.0 network.</li>
<li>The switch is limited to sending and receiving frames to and from the gateway 172.16.100.1.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>A default gateway address is typically configured on all devices to allow them to communicate beyond just their local network.In a switch this is achieved using the command ip default-gateway &lt;ip address&gt;.</p>

<h3>Which three commands are used to set up secure access to a router through a connection to the console interface? (Choose three.)</h3>
<ul>
<li>interface fastethernet 0/0</li>
<li>line vty 0 4</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">line console 0</span></li>
<li>enable secret cisco</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">login</span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">password cisco</span><br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The three commands needed to password protect the console port are as follows:<br />
line console 0<br />
password cisco<br />
login<br />
The interface fastethernet 0/0 command is commonly used to access the configuration mode used to apply specific parameters such as the IP address to the Fa0/0 port. The line vty 0 4 command is used to access the configuration mode for Telnet. The 0 and 4 parameters specify ports 0 through 4, or a maximum of five simultaneous Telnet connections. The enable secret command is used to apply a password used on the router to access the privileged mode.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>

<h3>Refer to the exhibit. Consider the IP address configuration shown from PC1. What is a description of the default gateway address?</h3>
<figure id="attachment_225" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-225" style="width: 612px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-225" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20612%20408'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="CCNA1 v7 - ITNv7 - Modules 8 - 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 01" width="612" height="408" data-lazy-srcset="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-01-1.jpg 612w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-01-1-300x200.jpg 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 612px) 100vw, 612px" data-lazy-src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-01-1.jpg" /><noscript><img decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-225" src="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-01-1.jpg" alt="CCNA1 v7 - ITNv7 - Modules 8 - 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 01" width="612" height="408" srcset="https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-01-1.jpg 612w, https://infraexam.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/CCNA1-v7-ITNv7-Modules-8-10-Communicating-Between-Networks-Exam-Answers-01-1-300x200.jpg 300w" sizes="(max-width: 612px) 100vw, 612px" /></noscript><figcaption id="caption-attachment-225" class="wp-caption-text">CCNA1 v7 &#8211; ITNv7 &#8211; Modules 8 &#8211; 10 Communicating Between Networks Exam Answers 01</figcaption></figure>
<ul>
<li>It is the IP address of the Router1 interface that connects the company to the Internet.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">It is the IP address of the Router1 interface that connects the PC1 LAN to Router1.</span></li>
<li>It is the IP address of Switch1 that connects PC1 to other devices on the same LAN.</li>
<li>It is the IP address of the ISP network device located in the cloud.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The default gateway is used to route packets destined for remote networks. The default gateway IP address is the address of the first Layer 3 device (the router interface) that connects to the same network.</p>

<h3>Which two functions are primary functions of a router? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">packet forwarding</span></li>
<li>microsegmentation</li>
<li>domain name resolution</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">path selection</span></li>
<li>flow control<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>A router accepts a packet and accesses its routing table to determine the appropriate exit interface based on the destination address. The router then forwards the packet out of that interface.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>

<li>
<h3>What is the effect of using the Router# copy running-config startup-config command on a router?</h3>
<ul>
<li>The contents of ROM will change.</li>
<li>The contents of RAM will change.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The contents of NVRAM will change.</span></li>
<li>The contents of flash will change.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The command copy running-config startup-config copies the running-configuration file from RAM into NVRAM and saves it as the startup-configuration file. Since NVRAM is none-volatile memory it will be able to retain the configuration details when the router is powered off.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What will happen if the default gateway address is incorrectly configured on a host?</h3>
<ul>
<li>The host cannot communicate with other hosts in the local network.</li>
<li>The switch will not forward packets initiated by the host.</li>
<li>The host will have to use ARP to determine the correct address of the default gateway.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The host cannot communicate with hosts in other networks.</span></li>
<li>A ping from the host to 127.0.0.1 would not be successful.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>When a host needs to send a message to another host located on the same network, it can forward the message directly. However, when a host needs to send a message to a remote network, it must use the router, also known as the default gateway. This is because the data link frame address of the remote destination host cannot be used directly. Instead, the IP packet has to be sent to the router (default gateway) and the router will forward the packet toward its destination. Therefore, if the default gateway is incorrectly configured, the host can communicate with other hosts on the same network, but not with hosts on remote networks.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What are two potential network problems that can result from ARP operation? (Choose two.)</h3>
<ul>
<li>Manually configuring static ARP associations could facilitate ARP poisoning or MAC address spoofing.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">On large networks with low bandwidth, multiple ARP broadcasts could cause data communication delays. </span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Network attackers could manipulate MAC address and IP address mappings in ARP messages with the intent of intercepting network traffic.</span></li>
<li>Large numbers of ARP request broadcasts could cause the host MAC address table to overflow and prevent the host from communicating on the network.</li>
<li>Multiple ARP replies result in the switch MAC address table containing entries that match the MAC addresses of hosts that are connected to the relevant switch port.<br />
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>Large numbers of ARP broadcast messages could cause momentary data communications delays. Network attackers could manipulate MAC address and IP address mappings in ARP messages with the intent to intercept network traffic. ARP requests and replies cause entries to be made into the ARP table, not the MAC address table. ARP table overflows are very unlikely. Manually configuring static ARP associations is a way to prevent, not facilitate, ARP poisoning and MAC address spoofing. Multiple ARP replies resulting in the switch MAC address table containing entries that match the MAC addresses of connected nodes and are associated with the relevant switch port are required for normal switch frame forwarding operations. It is not an ARP caused network problem.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
</ul>
</li>

<h3>Which interfaces in each router are active and operational?</h3>
<ul>
<li>R1:  G0/0 and S0/0/0<br />
R2:  G0/0 and S0/0/0</li>
<li>R1:  G0/1 and S0/0/1<br />
R2:  G0/0 and S0/0/1</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">R1: G0/0 and S0/0/0</span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;">R2: G0/1 and S0/0/0</span></li>
<li>R1: G0/0 and S0/0/1<br />
R2: G0/1 and S0/0/1</p>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr bgcolor="#e7f7e1">
<td>
<p><b>Answers Explanation &amp; Hints:</b></p>
<p>The command to use for this activity is show ip interface brief in each router. The active and operational interfaces are represented by the value &#8220;up&#8221; in the &#8220;Status&#8221; and &#8220;Protocol&#8221; columns. The interfaces in R1 with these characteristics are G0/0 and S0/0/0. In R2 they are G0/1 and S0/0/0.</p>

<ul>

<li>destination IPv4 address</li>
<li>source IPv4 address</li>
<li>TTL</li>
</ul>

<li>
<h3>What property of ARP causes cached IP-to-MAC mappings to remain in memory longer?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Entries in an ARP table are time-stamped and are purged after the timeout expires.</span></li>
<li>A static IP-to-MAC address entry can be entered manually into an ARP table.</li>
<li>The type field 0x806 appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The port-to-MAC address table on a switch has the same entries as the ARP table on the switch.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What property of ARP allows MAC addresses of frequently used servers to be fixed in the ARP table?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">A static IP-to-MAC address entry can be entered manually into an ARP table.</span></li>
<li>Entries in an ARP table are time-stamped and are purged after the timeout expires.</li>
<li>The type field 0x806 appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The port-to-MAC address table on a switch has the same entries as the ARP table on the switch.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What property of ARP allows MAC addresses of frequently used servers to be fixed in the ARP table?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">A static IP-to-MAC address entry can be entered manually into an ARP table.</span></li>
<li>The destination MAC address FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The source MAC address appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The port-to-MAC address table on a switch has the same entries as the ARP table on the switch.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What property of ARP allows hosts on a LAN to send traffic to remote networks?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Local hosts learn the MAC address of the default gateway.</span></li>
<li>The destination MAC address FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The source MAC address appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The port-to-MAC address table on a switch has the same entries as the ARP table on the switch.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What property of ARP allows hosts on a LAN to send traffic to remote networks?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">Local hosts learn the MAC address of the default gateway.</span></li>
<li>The destination MAC address FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The source MAC address appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>ARP replies are broadcast on the network when a host receives an ARP request.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What property of ARP forces all Ethernet NICs to process an ARP request?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The destination MAC address FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</span></li>
<li>The source MAC address appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The type field 0x806 appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>ARP replies are broadcast on the network when a host receives an ARP request.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What property of ARP causes a reply only to the source sending an ARP request?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The source MAC address appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</span></li>
<li>The destination MAC address FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>The type field 0x806 appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>ARP replies are broadcast on the network when a host receives an ARP request.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What property of ARP causes the request to be flooded out all ports of a switch except for the port receiving the ARP request?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The destination MAC address FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</span></li>
<li>The type field 0x806 appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>Entries in an ARP table are time-stamped and are purged after the timeout expires.</li>
<li>ARP replies are broadcast on the network when a host receives an ARP request.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<h3>What property of ARP causes the NICs receiving an ARP request to pass the data portion of the Ethernet frame to the ARP process?</h3>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;">The type field 0x806 appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</span></li>
<li>The destination MAC address FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>
<li>Entries in an ARP table are time-stamped and are purged after the timeout expires.</li>
<li>ARP replies are broadcast on the network when a host receives an ARP request.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li>The destination MAC address FF-FF-FF-FF-FF-FF appears in the header of the Ethernet frame.</li>

<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# no shutdown </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# interface gi0/0 </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# description Connects to the Engineering LAN </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# ip address 192.168.166.46 255.255.255.0 </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# no shutdown </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# interface s0/0/0 </span><br />

<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# ip address 10.166.167.254 255.255.255.0 </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# no shutdown </span><br />

<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# description Connects to the Head Office WAN </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# ip address 198.51.100.189 255.255.255.0 </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# no shutdown </span><br />
<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Main(config-if)# end</span></>
